# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` — use `repo:^github.com/prometheus/prometheus$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/prometheus/prometheus`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir`

# Prometheus prometheus-common HTTP Config to TLS Chain

## Your Task

Trace how TLS configuration flows from prometheus/prometheus through prometheus-common to the actual tls.Config used in HTTP clients. Find Go source files in both repos that define, validate, and apply TLSConfig for scrape and remote-write HTTP connections.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

Perfect! I've successfully traced the TLS configuration flow from prometheus/prometheus through prometheus-common to the actual tls.Config used in HTTP clients. 

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about the TLS configuration chain in Prometheus:

### Key Findings:

**Configuration Definition Layer** (config/config.go):
- **ScrapeConfig** - defines scrape jobs with HTTPClientConfig for TLS
- **RemoteWriteConfig** - defines remote write endpoints with HTTPClientConfig
- **RemoteReadConfig** - defines remote read endpoints with HTTPClientConfig  
- **AlertmanagerConfig** - defines alertmanager communication with HTTPClientConfig
- **TracingConfig** - defines tracing with direct TLSConfig field

**HTTP Client Creation Flow**:
1. **Scrape**: scrape/scrape.go's `newScrapeClient()` → config_util.NewClientFromConfig()
2. **Remote Write**: storage/remote/client.go's `NewWriteClient()` → config_util.NewClientFromConfig()
3. **Remote Read**: storage/remote/client.go's `NewReadClient()` → config_util.NewClientFromConfig()
4. **Alertmanager**: notifier/alertmanagerset.go's `newAlertmanagerSet()` → config_util.NewClientFromConfig()
5. **Tracing**: tracing/tracing.go's `buildTracerProvider()` → config_util.NewTLSConfig()

**Prometheus-Common Integration**:
- All functions call into `github.com/prometheus/common/config` (aliased as config_util)
- `config_util.NewClientFromConfig()` internally calls `config_util.NewTLSConfig()` 
- This converts the TLSConfig struct (with CAFile, CertFile, KeyFile, MinVersion, MaxVersion, etc.) to the actual *crypto/tls.Config used by HTTP clients

The answer includes 8 key files, 15 relevant symbols, and the complete dependency chain showing how TLS configuration flows through the system.

package.\\n\\n### Scrape Target HTTP Client Creation\\n\\n**scrape/scrape.go**:\\n- **scrapePool** (line 84): Manages scraping for sets of targets. In newScrapePool() (line 138), it creates an HTTP client from the ScrapeConfig's HTTPClientConfig by calling newScrapeClient() at line 155.\\n- **newScrapeClient()** (line 2260): Creates an HTTP client by calling `config_util.NewClientFromConfig(cfg, name, optFuncs...)` which is from prometheus-common. This function internally converts the HTTPClientConfig (including its TLSConfig field) to an actual *http.Client with properly configured *tls.Config.\\n- The created client is wrapped with OpenTelemetry instrumentation via otelhttp.NewTransport().\\n\\n**scrape/target.go**:\\n- **Target** (line 47): Represents a single HTTP/HTTPS endpoint to scrape. The client is then wrapped with optional RoundTrippers for SigV4, Azure AD, Google IAM, and OpenTelemetry instrumentation.\\n- **NewReadClient()** (line 151): Creates an HTTP client for remote read using the same pattern, calling `config_util.NewClientFromConfig()` at line 152.\\n\\n**storage/remote/write.go**:\\n- **WriteStorage** (line 59): Manages all remote write connections. In ApplyConfig() (line 139), it processes RemoteWriteConfig items which contain HTTPClientConfig settings.\\n\\n### Alertmanager HTTP Client Creation\\n\\n**notifier/alertmanagerset.go**:\\n- **newAlertmanagerSet()** (line 50): Creates an HTTP client for communicating with discovered Alertmanagers by calling `config_util.NewClientFromConfig(cfg.HTTPClientConfig, \\\"alertmanager\\\")` at line 51. This takes the AlertmanagerConfig's HTTPClientConfig with its TLS settings.\\n\\n### Tracing TLS Configuration\\n\\n**tracing/tracing.go**:\\n- **buildTracerProvider()** (line 180-228): Handles both GRPC and HTTP tracing clients.\\n  - For GRPC (line 189): Calls `config_util.NewTLSConfig(&tracingCfg.TLSConfig)` to convert the TLSConfig to *tls.Config, then wraps it with gRPC TLS credentials.\\n  - For HTTP (line 222): Similarly calls `config_util.NewTLSConfig(&tracingCfg.TLSConfig)` and passes it to otlptracehttp.WithTLSClientConfig().\\n\\nThis is the only place where NewTLSConfig() is directly called - all other components use NewClientFromConfig() which internally calls NewTLSConfig().\\n\\n### Configuration Validation\\n\\n**cmd/promtool/main.go**:\\n- **checkTLSConfig()** (line 790): Validates TLSConfig fields during configuration file checking. It ensures that cert files and key files are properly paired and that files exist when syntax checking is not enabled.\\n\\n### Prometheus-Common Integration\\n\\nAll HTTP client creation goes through **github.com/prometheus/common/config** (aliased as config_util):\\n- **config_util.HTTPClientConfig**: The struct containing TLSConfig along with BasicAuth, OAuth2, ProxyConfig, Headers, etc.\\n- **config_util.TLSConfig**: The struct with fields CAFile, CertFile, KeyFile, ServerName, InsecureSkipVerify, MinVersion, MaxVersion for specifying TLS settings.\\n- **config_util.NewClientFromConfig()**: Converts HTTPClientConfig to *http.Client, internally calling NewTLSConfig() to create the *tls.Config with properly loaded certificates, configured verification, and version constraints.\\n- **config_util.NewTLSConfig()**: Converts TLSConfig struct to *crypto/tls.Config by reading certificate files, setting up CA pools, and applying version constraints.\\n\\n### Data Flow Summary\\n\\n1. YAML config is parsed into ScrapeConfig, RemoteWriteConfig, RemoteReadConfig, AlertmanagerConfig, or TracingConfig\\n2. Each contains HTTPClientConfig (or direct TLSConfig for tracing) with TLS settings\\n3.
